“Dohee said that too.”

The new appointee stopped.

“Sir?”

“And three months later there was an incident.”

The new appointee paused a moment.

“…I will record it.”

“Do.”

Gadeung looked at the file again.

The new appointee started to leave and came back.

“By regulation there is no problem.”

“That means the regulation has no problem.”

“…Yes.”

“It does not mean reality has no problem.”

The new appointee left again.

-----

It was an upper-level briefing.

The upper floors of the Hwagam inspectorate. People of higher rank than Gadeung were there.

“Is there evidence concerning Sector 7.”

“Not yet.”

“Then close it.”

Gadeung heard it.

“There is an anomalous pattern. Abnormal on the summed basis.”

“Is it not within the normal range by the manual.”

“Individually, it is.”

“Then close it. Eidos and Altair have already entered on their own judgment. Hwagam follows regulation.”

Gadeung did not answer.

“Gadeung.”

“There is a record.”

“What record.”

“The 7-7-4 pattern is repeating. It was the same form before.”

The superior paused a moment.

“That time, Dohee found it.”

“Yes.”

“Dohee was dismissed.”

“That is correct.”

“Is the pattern returning a statement that Dohee was right.”

Gadeung heard the question. It could not be answered easily.

“Whether Dohee was right is still too early to judge,” Gadeung said. “But that Dohee saw it first, from outside the rules, is fact. Now I am seeing the same thing from inside the rules.”

The superior looked at Gadeung.

“What is your conclusion.”

“I will keep recording.”

The superior said no more. The closing order was not rescinded. But no further order came either.

-----

Gadeung looked at the file alone.

That the quality of Hwagam’s reports had changed since Dohee’s dismissal — Gadeung knew it. Changed did not mean worsened. The format had grown more exact. Manual compliance had risen.

But this pattern Gadeung had found — would he have found it without Dohee.

It was Dohee who first discovered 7-7-4. After Dohee’s dismissal, the same pattern recurred, and no one found it first. Gadeung had found it now. Because the 7-7-4 file was in the archive and could be compared.

Dohee’s record had helped Gadeung.

Gadeung thought about it. Dohee had broken the rules. Had been dismissed. And what Dohee left behind was doing the work now.

What was left from outside the rules.

Gadeung took out the notebook. The black notebook. The one for recording the things that were not official reports. 7-7-4 pattern recurrence. Summed abnormality. Upper-level closing order. Gadeung continuing independently.

Having written it, he opened the report again. The entries concerning Sector 7. Personnel concentration increasing. Hwagam, Eidos, Altair, Geumhui. Each in the same direction for different reasons.

Probability of collision rising.

He wrote it.

“What Dohee saw has come again.”

And one line more.

“This time, I see it from inside the rules.”

And one line more.

“I do not yet know the reason.”

-----

Inside the Echo Core, Dohee held the logbook.

There was the second page. The first line showed. Dohee knew her gaze was going there.

In this place — inside this structure — the logbook was different. Not heavy. Something seemed to be connecting.

Dohee read the first sentence of the second page.

She did not understand it.

So she closed it. That reading without understanding and closing without understanding were different — Dohee knew that. Having read it. That was the difference. Letters once read remained somewhere. Understanding was a thing that followed later. The 0.003 percent had been like that. At first it was a number, and later it became a door.

-----

*Ch.50 “The Recorder” — end*

-----

## Vol.6 — Ch.51 “Collision”

-----

The Hwagam advance unit reached the boundary.

Twelve of them. Hwagam’s manner of moving was always the same — a straight line. With a target, they took the fastest route. They did not detour. Hwagam’s execution arts were designed that way. Fast, linear, specialized for arrest.

The advance leader stood at the front.

A Geumhui boundary squad was blocking the way. Not blocking — standing. They held no weapons. Took no stances. They were simply in their places.

“Step aside.”

The advance leader said.

“There are no grounds.”

One of the Geumhui boundary squad said.

“This is execution.”

“The grounds for execution.”

The advance leader stopped. To Hwagam, execution was an order. When the upper ranks ordered execution, you executed. Asking for grounds was not the Hwagam way. And Geumhui kept asking for grounds.

“It is the Observer pursuit. Entry into Sector 7 confirmed. That is sufficient.”

“Has it been confirmed what the Observer did.”

“That they are here has been confirmed.”

“Being here is not grounds for execution.”

The advance leader listened no further.

“We enter.”

-----

Hwagam moved.

Fast. Twelve moved at once. Not in different directions — the same direction. They concentrated on one member of the boundary squad. The Hwagam way. Punching through one point fast. Making a weak point, and passing everyone through it.

The Geumhui boundary squad stepped back.

They did not block. They stepped back. Hwagam went in through the gap. They succeeded in entering — so it looked.

But the place they entered was closed.

Two of the Geumhui boundary squad were already in that place. It was not the place Hwagam had punched into — Geumhui had sent Hwagam to that place. By controlling the direction of the stepping-back, they had made Hwagam go not where Hwagam wanted but where Geumhui meant to send them.

The advance leader realized it.

“They are building a boundary.”

Geumhui did not block Hwagam. It decided where Hwagam could go and where it could not. Narrowing the passages, restricting the directions, in the end shrinking the very space in which Hwagam could move.

The advance leader ordered again.

“Scatter. Several directions at once.”

The twelve of Hwagam scattered. Six directions. The Geumhui boundary squad numbered fewer. They could not block them all.

They did not block.

“Record.”

One of the boundary squad said.

In that moment, the Geumhui boundary squad moved to predetermined positions. The six directions Hwagam had scattered into — where those directions finally met, Geumhui knew. Hwagam had not scattered. They had scattered into the six directions Geumhui had predicted. At the meeting point, Geumhui was there.

Six of Hwagam gathered at the same place. They had scattered, and gathered.

The advance leader stopped.

Then — two of the boundary squad were subdued at once.

It was not the advance leader. Two of Hwagam who had been behind moved simultaneously. A direction Geumhui had not predicted. Two of the boundary squad were taken. For the first time, Geumhui departed from its plan.

Through that gap, three of Hwagam punched in.

Muyul saw it.

“One minute.”

The subordinate went rigid.

-----

There was a brief engagement.

Hwagam attempted a forced breakthrough. They collided directly with the Geumhui boundary squad. Hwagam’s execution arts were specialized for subdual — neutralizing an opponent fast and arresting them. One of the Geumhui boundary squad was taken. Subdued.

But the taken squad member did not resist.

Being taken, he shifted position. Not taken — he had drawn Hwagam in along the direction of the taking. While Hwagam concentrated on subduing him, the other squad members closed Hwagam’s line of retreat.

A gun fired. One round. A warning. Fired upward.

A window broke. One in the structure’s outer wall. Fragments fell.

One of the Geumhui boundary squad was struck by a fragment. Near the eye. He put a hand to his face. The hand was red. It was not severe — the fragment had grazed. He had not lost his sight. But the feeling of something caught in the right field of vision persisted.

It was Seoan. The youngest of the Geumhui boundary squad.

“Are you all right.”

Another squad member asked.

“Recording.”

Seoan said. He lowered his hand. He kept his place.

One of Hwagam was scratched on the arm. That was all. No one died. No one was badly hurt. On the skin beside Seoan’s eye, the fragment’s trace remained. A thin scar.

Not one of the Geumhui boundary squad used a lethal weapon. Neither did Hwagam. Every house had the same rule — killing without authorization was forbidden. There was no order to kill. Subdue, isolate, neutralize, arrest. That was all.

The advance leader took in the situation.

All twelve of Hwagam were inside a controlled space. They could move — and there was nowhere to move. It was not that Geumhui had sealed the whole space. They had known in advance every direction Hwagam would try, and stood at the end of each.

“Is this the Geumhui way.”

The advance leader said.

“Order is not blocking,” the boundary squad member said. “It is deciding where one can go.”

-----

Muyul received the report outside the boundary.

“Twelve of Hwagam have entered. Under control.”

“I know.”

“There was an attempted forced breakthrough.”

“I know.”

The subordinate paused a moment.

“Since when have you known.”

Muyul looked at the subordinate.

“Kangwi recorded it yesterday.”

The subordinate heard it. Yesterday. Hwagam had entered today, and Kangwi had recorded this yesterday. That Hwagam would come, from which direction it would come — Kangwi had known in advance.

“Two minutes.”

Muyul said.

“What is.”

“The time for Hwagam to reach the Echo Core at their current rate of entry.”

The subordinate stopped.

“We must stop them.”

“We are recording.”

Muyul looked at the boundary. Hwagam was inside the controlled space. He did not execute. There were as yet no grounds for execution. He did not block. There was no reason to block. He was simply recording what Hwagam did.

Once he knew what Hwagam meant to do, that became grounds for execution. Until then, it was recording.

“Keep recording.”

Muyul said.

-----

Inside the Echo Core, something else was underway.

The sound of the engagement outside could be heard. It was far. Hangyeol held the entrance. He sent ARIA deeper in. Dohee and that person were further inside.

Hangyeol looked out from the entrance.

“Someone’s coming.”

Dohee looked that way.

“Hwagam?”

“I don’t know. But it’s several people.”

That person listened to the sounds outside.

“Faster than expected.”

They said it low. Dohee looked at them. Faster than whom, faster than what — Dohee did not ask.

Hangyeol closed his hand. He might have to fight. Until now, Hangyeol had run. This time there was nowhere to run. ARIA was inside. He had to protect ARIA.

But the sounds outside did not come closer.

The engagement was not coming toward the Echo Core. It was happening elsewhere. Someone over there was holding Hwagam. Keeping them from reaching the Echo Core.

Hangyeol did not know who it was. Thinking it fortunate — he also thought it strange.

-----

Inside, ARIA was looking at the wall.

Even at the sounds of the engagement she did not move. She stayed with her hand on the wall. Dohee came to her side.

“ARIA.”

“Yes.”

“Are you all right?”

“This.” ARIA pointed at the wall. “I think I might know what this is.”

Dohee looked at the wall. There was script. What was seen in R-02, what was seen at the Echo Sites, what was seen at the observation network. The three kinds, each in its own place.

“What is it.”

“This isn’t script.”

Dohee looked at her.

“Then what is it.”

ARIA paused a moment.

“It’s a record.”

The moment ARIA said it — a sound came from the wall. A vibration. Something seemed to move inside the structure. Beginning from the part ARIA’s hand touched, the three kinds of characters trembled at once. It was not light. It was movement. The carved things seemed to shift slightly in their places.

Everyone looked that way at once.

ARIA did not take her hand away.

“It’s what remained. Something happened — and that is what remained here.”

Dohee looked at the wall again.

Not script but record. Not written but remained. Something happened, and it was carved here.

Dohee thought of the logbook. It was in the pack. The first sentence of the second page, read and not understood. That logbook and this wall — could be the same thing.

Dohee had the thought, and did not yet say it.

-----

The engagement ended.

The Hwagam advance unit withdrew. Having confirmed they could not get out of the controlled space, they stopped forcing it. Geumhui did not pursue. Did not take them. It recorded Hwagam withdrawing.

The advance leader said, last:

“This becomes a problem later.”

“We will record it.”

Hwagam left.

The Geumhui boundary squad kept their places. They had not blocked, not taken, not killed. They had recorded everything Hwagam had tried to do. That was all Geumhui had done.

And it had been enough.

Muyul started to close the records.

In that moment.

A sound came from the direction of the Echo Core.

A sound heard for the first time. A sound like stone moving. It seemed to come from inside the structure, and seemed to come from the structure itself.

Muyul raised his head.

There was no agitation in the expression. Only the verdict of lateness. Geumhui’s time was the time of events, and the event had already passed.

“Too late, then.”

-----

*Ch.51 “Collision” — end*

-----

## Vol.6 — Ch.52 “Opening”

-----

The sound came first.

From the wall ARIA’s hand touched. A vibration. It could be felt through the soles of the feet. The floor seemed to move. It was not moving — the structure itself was responding.

Hangyeol moved in front of ARIA.

“Back.”

ARIA did not step back.

“Hangyeol.”

“Back, for now.”

“This isn’t dangerous.”

ARIA said. She said it as if certain. But hearing it, Hangyeol could not tell — certainty, or wishing.

The vibration grew.

From somewhere inside the structure came the sound of stone moving. Not loud. The sound of something changing its place. The sound of a thing long fixed moving for the first time.

And one part of the wall changed.

The wall did not vanish. A part of the wall became different. A space opened, leading inward. It was not newly made — what had been there from the start had opened. A place that had been closed had opened.

Dohee saw it.

-----

ARIA stopped.

After the wall responded, ARIA took her hand away. Took it away, and did not step back. She looked at the opened space. The newly opened side.

She said nothing.

Hangyeol stood beside her.

“ARIA.”

“Yes.”

“Do you think you know?”

ARIA paused a moment. Usually, what came out would have been I don’t know, or I think I might know, or I just know. One of the three. This time it was different.

“I’m scared.”

Hangyeol looked at her.

It was a first. ARIA saying she was scared. She had said she didn’t know. She had said she was bewildered. Scared — it was the first time.

“Why.”

“I don’t know. This place feels like something I know — and it might not be. I’d never thought that what feels known could be wrong.”

Hangyeol heard it.

For the first time, ARIA had thought she could be wrong. That was what scared her.

Hangyeol understood it. ARIA knew the direction, and Hangyeol followed the direction. The relation rested on that. If ARIA’s sense of direction wavered — there was no direction for Hangyeol to follow.

“It’s all right.”

Hangyeol said.

“Even if I’m wrong?”

“Even if you’re wrong.”

ARIA looked at him.

“How.”

“Just because.”

Hangyeol looked toward the opened space. Whatever it was, it seemed they had to go in. This was not the place to stop. Even if ARIA was scared, even if the direction wavered — what could be done now had to be done.

“Do we go in?”

ARIA looked at the opened space.

She was scared. There was something she half knew and could not know. That she could be wrong — she felt it for the first time.

Still, she nodded.

“Yes.”

-----

Dohee took out the logbook.

It was now. It was this place. She had read the first sentence of the second page and not understood it. Had closed it without understanding. And had come to this place.

She opened it.

The second page. There was the first sentence. The one read once. The one not understood.

She read it again.

*We leave records. Not in order to remember. Because it repeats.*

Dohee read it.

Repetition. Not memory — repetition. Not recording in order to remember, but recording because it repeats. Dohee looked at it for a long time.

What was it that repeats. That this question repeats. That this situation repeats. That this place repeats. That it has been recorded many times — that the same thing has happened many times.

She looked at the next sentence.

*If you see this when you come next, that is the proof that the repetition has occurred.*

Dohee stopped.

When you come next. The one who comes next. This logbook had been written for someone who would come next. Dohee was that next person.

Before her, too, this place had been here. This structure had been here. This logbook had been here. And someone came. And recorded. And Dohee came.

It was repetition.

Dohee did not close the logbook.

-----

That person was beside Dohee.

They did not look at the logbook with her. They looked at the structure’s interior. Looked at the opened space. Looked long.

Dohee said:

“You said it was too late.”

That person looked at her.

“What was too late.”

That person paused a moment.

“This time too.”

Dohee heard it. This time too. That there had been times other than this one. That at this same place, before, the same words had been said.

“Have you come here before.”

That person did not answer.

Dohee looked at the logbook. *If you see this when you come next, that is the proof that the repetition has occurred.*

If that person had come before — they would have seen this logbook. Or they would have been the one who left it.

Dohee did not say it. Did not ask. Not now.

“What happens next.”

That person looked at the opened space.

“I don’t know.”

Dohee heard it.

“Do you think this time will be different.”

That person paused a moment.

“I don’t know.”

“Then why come.”

That person looked at her.

“If I don’t come, it ends faster.”

Dohee heard the words. She could ask no further.

-----

Outside, Muyul received a report.

“The Echo Core entrance has changed. Entry impossible.”

Muyul looked that way. The structure’s outer wall had become different. The place one could have entered was gone. There was no new entrance. The entrance itself had vanished.

Eidos came.

It was Tiko. He came from far off and said nothing. He looked at the structure. Looked long. It was observing.

Altair came.

It was Claire. The moment Claire arrived she took out the calculator. She tried to quantify the change in the structure’s outer wall. No figures came out. Claire stopped.

From the Eidos direction, one more came.

It was Min Siwoo. He held the Observer’s lens. He looked at the structure. Looked from far off. Did not go near. Wanting to go near, and not going.

He raised the lens. The cracked one. The one that could not be seen through.

But this time, for a moment, something seemed to show. The structure’s interior. He could not be certain. It might have been the eye’s illusion. He held it up anyway.

Four camps stood before the same structure. None could enter.

Muyul maintained the boundary. There were no grounds for execution. What the structure was could not yet be known. Not knowing, he did not execute.

Tiko stood beside Muyul.

“What happened.”

“Recording.”

“What kind of record do you think it will become.”

“I don’t know.”

Tiko looked at the structure.

“Then it isn’t observation either.”

Muyul looked at Tiko. Eidos admitting that observation was impossible — it was the first time Muyul had heard such words.

Tiko had not said it to Muyul. He had simply said it.

-----

Inside the Echo Core, the wall moved.

It was not that a door opened. What had not originally been a door — began to look like one.

ARIA walked toward it.

Hangyeol followed. Whatever it was. Wherever it led.

Dohee put the logbook in the pack. There was still no answer. One more question had formed. That was enough.

That person went ahead.

The four moved. Four sets of footsteps gathered into one direction. It was not the rhythm of people who had walked together from the start. But it did not fall out of step either. It was a rhythm in the middle of being matched.

-----

*Ch.52 “Opening” — end*

-----

*Opening: Kangwi placed his hand on the board*
*Closing: the Echo Core responded*
